  100. FYI: Authentic African Black Soap is not supposed to be black. It is supposed to be brown. Soaps claiming to be ABS and are black are not authentic, even though they may work perfectly fine for some people. They are typically just dyed soaps. If those products work for you, then great! If you want the authentic stuff, this is it.<br />Before I tried this soap, I tried Dudu Osun for several months. There is a slight scent to this one, but it's not as strong as Dudu Osun. The package came in a plastic wrap when I opened the box and WOW. This block is huge, and the soap is malleable, meaning that you can pull it apart and break it into pieces if you want.It's almost kinda squishy. I really love how little pieces last forever. Like with any ABS, it will dissolve in water if you let it sit in it; if you like to melt it down or make your own liquid soap, then this is great but if you want to avoid any melting, then store it in a soap dish.<br />This soap is drying, but it is tolerable as long as you have a very good moisturizer. Sometimes I wash my face with a few drops of tea tree oil and this soap in order to remove some dark spots, but that is more of a personal thing I like to do. By itself, it's very good for drying out blemishes. If you're looking for deep exfoliation, this soap is great for that; youcould even take it a step further and use an exfoliation pad. There are some tiny grains in mine, but they haven't hurt me like some people have complained. I haven't found any hairs in my batch either. I've had this soap for a little over a month and still have about 80-90% of it left, but this is only because a little goes a very long way. I'll definitely purchase this again. It's cost-effective and works incredibly well.

  262. I had to write a review on this because I had such high hopes for it and I thought I had done my research on this stuff beforehand but I've learned things first hand about using this soap and its effect on my skin.<br /><br />First most, I am certain that Amazon and the seller did their part on selling me and shipping me 100% pure African black soap, it came packaged in plastic in one giant chunk, and two smaller chunks. It is raw, so it means it is completely unprocessed, so that means there is still going to be sediment in it from the process it takes to make this soap.<br /><br />This sediment, some people on here think it's hair and get freaked out, but i think it's ash or fibres from the plantain skins. They are extremely rough and have left me with scratches all over my body. I didn't believe it could actually leave scratches despite feeling that the soap was rough ,I thought my partner has just been extra rough during frickle frackle so it didn't bother but then i attributed it to the soap when i found circular scratches on my buttocks that look more like a satanic symbol that it does look like love scratches. That's when I knew I knew it was the black soap- I had a flash memory of rubbing the soap in circular motions on my buttocks with reckless abandon.<br /><br />I used it on my face at first, which was my original intention. I heard so many raves about it being really great for the skin (I have sensitive, oily, highly acne-prone skin with P.I.H.) and leaving peoples skin soft like butter and potentially being good for diminishing hyper pigmentation due to it's shea butter content. I was hearing about it everywhere- even when I didn't want to. In the most unexpected of places too, I was watching some speech at some event Obama had at the white house on youtube and this person was talking about African black soap. I stopped using it on my face when I found out ABS is extremely alkaline/basic. It has a P.H of 10+. higher than that of Dove Soap. So essentially, ABS is worse than Dove Soap (On the same P.H level as Baking Soda, which is a big no-no for use on the skin_, and Dove Soap irks the living jeebus out of my body skin, let alone my facial skin. The reason why P.H is important because in order for your skin to carry out its functions and be healthy (including the acid mantle/ moisture barrier) it has to maintain it's natural, acidic, P.H of around 4. It's advise you don't use a cleanser on your skin that has a P.H higher of 6, and then tone afterwards with a toner with a lower P.H to balance the P.H of skin. Also when I used this soap on my face, I didn't apply it directly because I knew it would scratch up my skin (IDK why i thought my body skin wouldn't get scratched up) so I would lather it up in my hand and then wash my face with the lather I had created. This soap has a good lather, but what else would you expect with something with such a high P.H<br /><br />I tried using it on my hair once and although it provided a good lather on my head, my hair got gummy, dry, and gross.<br /><br />For now I'm going to stop using it on my body (I have already since stopped using it on my face) as I feel it's my exacerbating my body acne (It's at its worse at this point) and dries out my skin. I would rather not have a bunch of tiny, even big scratches all over my skin. I'm thinking of liquefying it and just using it to wash my hands and feet.<br /><br />This soap also can get really messy and soft easily, If you leave it in moisture/water too long it gets for a gooey, putty like consistency and you end up washing away most of the soap. You have to use it in small chunks at a time and it keep it in a dry container to keep from wasting it.<br /><br />It doesn't smell particular of anything, just a naturally, earthy scent as others describe it. I'm actually a huge fan of scents like this but couldn't be bothered to like the scent of this stuff. It's nothing too strong that would irritate people sensitive to smells.<br /><br />Overall, I would not recommend this to anyone seeing how alkaline it is, unless you are a bar of soap I wouldn't recommend you wash your body with this

  411. Just got this yesterday and everything is as expected. For those of you who are not familiar with this kind of soap, cut it into small pieces and store them in a zip lock bag, using a little bit at a time. Given the nature of this kind of soap, you may not want to rub the bar directly onto your skin since the particles can cause abrasions (this is normal for raw black soaps). If you store any kind of authentic black soap in a wet area, it will absorb water and melt, and that is not indicative of a low quality soap. Also, the white film that can sometimes develop is NOT mold and if it you see it form, just know it's due to exposure to air and the soap is still ok to use.

  576. I was a bit concerned about buying this product from King of Natural Product, as people were complaining consistently about sticks being in the soap and how it came packaged. However, having received the block of soap and broken it down into small balls, I can say that the people giving this soap low reviews just are not people who regularly use this soap.<br /><br />Raw African Black Soap will melt. It will melt with very little water on it and it'll melt a little after you use it to lather up and set it down. That's the nature of the soap and you aren't doing anything wrong if this happens. On the same note, the vendor has done nothing wrong if your black soap is melting like this. That is the nature of the product, hence most people cutting it into tiny balls to lather with. You waste less if you only wash with small chunks at a time. Also, do not place this in a soap holder that will contain standing water. Always set the soap aside on a dry counter when done or on a paper towel. Anything that will dry out and not just hold the water.<br /><br />The smell. Yes, this is an earthy soap. There is no fragrance in it. No true raw black soap has fragrance other than the natural earthy scent. It isn't strong and after rinsing, no one will smell your face and be turned off by it. This is the natural scent of the soap and not the vendor's problem or because you did anything wrong with it.<br /><br />A lot of people complained about getting crumbles instead of the solid bar. The vendor I used sent a solid bar. It did not meet the 16oz requirement, but I also understand why his/her measurements are off. The vendor is probably cutting from a 10 lb solid block and cutting another sliver from the block is very difficult to do. Since the vendor can't weigh it until the block has been removed, and the crumbles would look bad, we get an ounce less than described. Let me tell you, the cheapest vendor in my area or on any other site sells 10oz for 14 bucks. Even missing a few ounces, this is a steal. Also, if you get the soap in crumbles, just compress them in your hand. Voila! A solid block! No more worries, friend. Either way, it's best to break up the soap and use smaller compressed balls to wash with daily so that the soap lasts longer. A pound is more than enough to last you a year of daily use if you only wash your face with it.<br /><br />Last but not least, remember to lather with the soap. Don't rub it on your body. Lather in your hands and then spread the lather. It makes the soap last and prevents cutting if there are any solid bits in the soap (of which I found none).
